<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="b9455d2c8dd44dceac7376ff9da22e3a"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="b9455d2c8dd44dceac7376ff9da22e3a">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'cfc37f5c-7881-4514-ad61-af71f58f5042'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d140825990" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>The bimetallic synergies effect and combined conversion/alloying mechanism endow thiospinel FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> with great potential as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). However, their inconsistent synthesis, severe volumetric expansion, and sluggish reaction kinetics typically lead to unsatisfactory cyclic stability and rate capability. Herein, bimetallic organic framework derived FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@N/S-C microrods with Fe vacancies is presented for fast, durable, and reversible sodium storage. The presence of Fe vacancies significantly modulates the <i>d</i>-band center of Fe and decreases the strength of the Fe─S bond for facilitating the sodiation reaction kinetics jointly. Moreover, a thin and stable solid electrolyte interface film with inorganic-rich components is formed by Fe vacancies induction. Combined with the N, S co-doped porous carbon matrix, the optimal sample delivers an excellent rate capability of 381 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup> and a stable cyclic performance (448 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>). Furthermore, the assembled full-cells also exhibit superior electrochemical performance with 87.5% capacity retention after rate and long-term cyclic evaluations. This work presents a promising strategy for the structural regulation of bimetallic sulfides as advanced anodes for SIBs.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202405729-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202405729-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the potential alternatives to replace lithium-ion batteries in the field of electric vehicles and energy storage stations, owing to the fact that sodium with abundant resources, wide distribution, and similar chemical properties to lithium.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0001_R_d140825861e486" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">1</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0004_R_d140825861e486" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Adv. Mater.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, a large ionic radius of Na<sup>+</sup> leads to low energy density, sluggish reaction kinetics, and volumetric changes in electrode materials during the cycles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0005_R_d140825861e493" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Adv. Mater.">5</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0007_R_d140825861e493" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The graphite with small interlayer spacing typically used as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries cannot accommodate repeated de/intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0008_R_d140825861e501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">8</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0009_R_d140825861e501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Among the reported anode materials, In-based sulfides with the combined conversion and alloying Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism have garnered increasing attention due to their moderated metal-sulfur bond and high theoretical capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0010_R_d140825861e508" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Mater.">10</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0011_R_d140825861e508" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Next Energy">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, their potential electrocatalytic activity would accelerate the kinetics of the sodiation/desodiation reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0012_R_d140825861e514" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - J. Colloid. Interface. Sci.">12</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0013_R_d140825861e514" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Chem. Eng. J.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, indium sulfides also undergo the inevitable volumetric expansion during the sodiation/desodiation processes, which results in unsatisfactory cyclic stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0014_R_d140825861e519" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Nanoscale">14</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0016_R_d140825861e519" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This volume change caused by the alloy and conversion reaction mechanisms with Na<sup>+</sup> would expedite the pulverization of anode material, hinder the formation of stable solid electrolyte interface (SEI) film, and induce unfavorable side reactions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0017_R_d140825861e527" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - J. Mater. Chem. A">17</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0018_R_d140825861e527" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - J. Energy Chem.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Nowadays, bimetallic sulfides have attracted considerable research attention due to their abundant redox active sites, bimetallic synergies effect, and ionic diffusion channels, which usually result in an overall performance enhancement compared to corresponding monometallic sulfides.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0019_R_d140825861e534" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">19</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0021_R_d140825861e534" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - J. Power Sources">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Among indium-based bimetallic sulfides, CuInS<sub>2</sub><sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0022_R_d140825861e540" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - ACS Energy Lett.">22</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0023_R_d140825861e540" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - J. Colloid. Interface. Sci.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and ZnIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub><sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0024_R_d140825861e549" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - ACS Nano">24</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0026_R_d140825861e549" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Ceram. Int.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> exhibit improved cyclic stability and specific capacity, making them promising candidates as anode materials for SIBs. However, the tetragonal and hexagonal structures of CuInS<sub>2</sub> and ZnIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> seem to be unsuited for fast Na<sup>+</sup> storage. Thiospinel FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> with the stable and symmetric structure emerges as an even more suitable candidate.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0027_R_d140825861e567" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The introduction of iron atoms to replace indium atoms will enhance the proportion of conversion type sodium storage process in indium-based anode and relieve its mechanical strain, which is beneficial for the cyclic stability under elevated current density. Furthermore, the electrocatalysis of the iron component would promote the conversion of sodium polysulfide and boost the electrochemical kinetics of FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0028_R_d140825861e577" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">28</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0029_R_d140825861e577" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Adv. Energy Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This effect can be further amplified by regulating its structure and morphology, especially in the presence of vacancies and carbon layers.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0030_R_d140825861e582" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Adv. Powder Mater.">30</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0032_R_d140825861e582" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - SusMat">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the synthesis of FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@C is usually impeded by the volatility of sulfur, multivalence of iron, and reduction of the carbon layer during the heat-treatment process. Avoiding the formation of two separate metal sulfides is also a challenge for FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@C anode. Yang's group reported the spinel FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> nanosheets synthesized by an isomorphous substitution route using In<sub>2.77</sub>S<sub>4</sub> as a precursor, which delivered improved cyclic and rate performance than that of In<sub>2.77</sub>S<sub>4</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0027_R_d140825861e609" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Fan's group constructed a hierarchical structure of FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles anchored on MXene flakes by interface ion-exchange strategy.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0033_R_d140825861e619" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J. Colloid. Interface. Sci.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> MXene@In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> is also employed as a precursor to synthesize MXene@In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/FeS<sub>2</sub> intermediate, which is subsequently transformed into MXene@FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> through heat-treatment. The aforementioned methods necessitate intricate designs and multistep reactions, posing challenges to the consistency of synthesis.</p>
         
         <p>The regular crystal structure and tunable metal sites endow metal-organic frameworks (MOFs) with a significant competitive for synthesizing bimetallic sulfides.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0034_R_d140825861e642" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Chem. Eng. J.">34</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0037_R_d140825861e642" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Nano">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the different kinds of metal atoms can be easily and uniformly dispersed within the MOF precursor, while the organic ligand not only facilitates the formation of a carbon layer to enhance electrical conductivity but also prevents metal sulfide aggregation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0038_R_d140825861e647" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Rare Metal">38</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0039_R_d140825861e647" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Sci.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This strategy is anticipated to overcome the constraints of the isomorphous ion exchange method on the same crystal structure between the precursor and product. Recently, the presence of cation vacancies in host materials has been reported to be beneficial for improving electrochemical performances, by regulating electronic structure and facilitating electrons/ions transfer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0040_R_d140825861e652" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Adv. Energy Mater.">40</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0042_R_d140825861e652" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Appl. Energ. Mater.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In detail, the regulated electronic structure is usually caused by the shift in the <i>d</i>/<i>p</i>-band center of transition metals.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0043_R_d140825861e662" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Sci. Bull.">43</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0044_R_d140825861e662" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Energy Storage Mater.">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Inspired by the promising applications in the field of electrocatalysis, the conversion/alloying reaction of metal sulfides with Na<sup>+</sup>, as well as the transformation of sodium polysulfides are anticipated to be promoted by the modulated electronic orbits, thereby improving the electrochemical properties of the host materials.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0045_R_d140825861e670" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, it is worthwhile to develop a facile method for the synthesis of thiospinel FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> with cation vacancies, aiming at its potential application in advanced SIBs anode.</p>
         
         <p>Herein, thiospinel FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@N/S-C microrods with Fe vacancies are presented by using an In-Fe metal-organic framework (In-Fe-MOF) as the precursor. The uniform distribution of indium and iron atoms in MOF precursor is conducive to the formation of the bimetallic sulfides. During the sulfuration process, incomplete reduction of Fe<sup>3+</sup> by the carbon layer and thioacetamide induces the generation of Fe vacancies. For comparison, FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles without Fe vacancies are constructed by the solvothermal ion substitution route using In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@C as a precursor, which is obtained from the monometallic In-MOF. The presence of Fe vacancies not only elevates the Fe <i>d</i>-band center to regulate the electronic structure and enhance the Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption capability but also reduces the strength of Fe─S bonds, thereby facilitating the kinetics of sodiation reaction to improve the structural reversibility. Furthermore, Fe vacancies also induce a thin and inorganic-rich component SEI to enhance the cyclic stability. When employed as an anode material for SIBs, Fe vacancies-rich FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@N/S-C microrods deliver the high reversible capacity (611 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> with an initial Coulombic efficiency of 84.3%), excellent rate capability (381 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>), and stable cyclic performance (448 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>). In particular, the assembled full-cell with commercial Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode also exhibits durable cyclic performance with 94.7% capacity retention after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and 87.5% capacity retention after complex rate and cyclic test, indicating its prospect for advanced SIBs applications.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202405729-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202405729-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p><b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0001">1a</a> illustrates the overall conceptual preparation process in this work. In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@C (denoted as IS) originated from In-MOF is employed as the precursor to synthesize FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@C nanoparticles (denoted as FIS) by the solvothermal Fe<sup>2+</sup> substitution route according to the previous literature.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0027_R_d140825861e754" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0033_R_d140825861e754" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J. Colloid. Interface. Sci.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Innovatively, the In-Fe bimetallic MOF is synthesized by incorporating Fe<sup>3+</sup> during the preparation of In-MOF, followed by a one-step heat treatment to obtain FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@N/S-C microrods with Fe vacancies (denoted as FIS-V). Initially, Density Functional Theory (DFT) calculations are carried out to predict the sodium storage performances of the In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4,</sub> and iron-deficient FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> by constructing supercell structures of In<sub>24</sub>S<sub>32</sub>, Fe<sub>8</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32,</sub> and Fe<sub>7</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub>, respectively. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0001">1c,d</a>, the obvious density of states (DOS) discontinuity of In<sub>24</sub>S<sub>32</sub> is reduced by Fe substitution. Notably, the presence of an iron vacancy leads to a continuous electron distribution in Fe<sub>7</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0001">1d</a>), and its DOS at the Fermi level is highest among the counterparts, indicating a positive influence of iron vacancies on enhancing sample conductivity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0046_R_d140825861e813" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Adv. Energy Mater.">46</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0047_R_d140825861e813" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Chem. Eng. J.">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The state project density (pDOS) of Fe d orbital in Fe<sub>8</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub> manifests as an asymmetric distribution of spin up and spin down, which will be changed by removing a Fe atom (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0001">1e</a>). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0001">1f</a>, the Fe <i>d</i>-band center of Fe<sub>7</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub> exhibits a positive shift from -0.468 to -0.436&nbsp;eV in the presence of a Fe vacancy, thereby facilitating the Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption, electronic conductivity, and electron/ion transfer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0048_R_d140825861e842" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Int. J. Hydrog. Energy">48</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0050_R_d140825861e842" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0001">1g</a> depicts the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion energy barriers of the constructed models. With the introduction of iron atoms, the diffusion energy barrier of sodium ions in bimetallic sulfide is significantly lower than that of monometallic In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>. Furthermore, by strategically designing iron vacancies, the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion energy barrier can be further reduced, thereby facilitating rapid Na<sup>+</sup> transfer. The iron vacancies would play a role as Na<sup>+</sup> micropumps to push Na<sup>+</sup> into the surrounding lattice.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0051_R_d140825861e866" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Adv. Mater.">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0001">1h</a>, the difference in charge density of the three models displays the substantial electron redistribution around the Fe vacancy, indicating the enhancement in Na<sup>+</sup> adsorbed capability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0052_R_d140825861e877" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Chin. Chem. Lett.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Meanwhile, the lowest Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption energy of Fe<sub>7</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub> (−3.60&nbsp;eV) further demonstrates the strengthened Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption by the presence of Fe vacancy (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0001">1i</a>). In addition, the electron localization function (ELF) along the (011) plane of the two models exhibits a significant alteration around the S atoms due to the presence of Fe vacancy (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0001">1j,k</a>). The reduced electron pair density of Fe<sub>7</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub> demonstrates a decreased strength of the Fe─S bond, which would promote the broken of the Fe─S bond during the sodiation reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0053_R_d140825861e906" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Adv. Energy Mater.">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202405729-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/cca9b336-8fd7-45e9-b74b-6f85580a1c3d/aenm202405729-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/cca9b336-8fd7-45e9-b74b-6f85580a1c3d/aenm202405729-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/bd27cae0-32bb-4a27-9459-378374457fcd/aenm202405729-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/cca9b336-8fd7-45e9-b74b-6f85580a1c3d/aenm202405729-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202405729-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202405729" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic diagram of the preparation processes; density of states of b) In<sub>24</sub>S<sub>32</sub>, c) Fe<sub>8</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub> and d) Fe<sub>7</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub>; e) the pDOS of Fe-<i>d</i> orbitals; f) the shifting diagram of Fe <i>d</i>-band center; g) Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion energy barrier; h) the difference charge density of Na<sup>+</sup> adsorbed on different models, yellow, purple and brown balls represents S, In and Fe atoms, respectively; i) Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption energy; the electron localization function of j) Fe<sub>8</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub> and k) Fe<sub>7</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1a</a> (Supporting Information), the In-Fe MOF exhibits a regular microrod-like morphology with 3–8&nbsp;µm in width. After the sulfuration process, FIS-V displays the monodispersed microrod-like morphology with the porous surface, which originated from precursors inheritance and thermal decomposition of organic ligands, respectively (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0002">2a,b</a>). The magnified scanning electron microscope (SEM)&nbsp;image (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0002">2c</a>) reveals that these microrods are assembled by numerous primary particles with obvious voids, thereby facilitating an enhanced contact area between the active materials and electrolytes. Interestingly, the monometallic In-MOF presents a combined morphology of microrods and microspheres, leading to a hybrid microrod- and spherical-like morphology in In-MOF-derived In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@C (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1b,c</a>, Supporting Information). After solvothermal Fe<sup>2+</sup> substitution and secondary heat treatment, both the microrods and microspheres have undergone fracture, resulting in the formation of irregular nanoparticles in the FIS (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0002">2d</a>). The transmission electron microscope (TEM) image of FIS-V shows a porous and quasi-hollow microrod-like structure, consistent with the SEM results (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0002">2e</a>). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0002">2f,g</a>, the high-resolution transmission electron microscope (HRTEM)&nbsp;images of FIS-V show distinct lattice fringes with a spacing of 0.37&nbsp;nm. Combined with the selected area electron diffraction (SAED) pattern from [111] direction (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0002">2h</a>), these lattice fringes with angles of 120° can be identified as (2_02) and (2_20) crystal planes in cubic <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/0c364656-cf98-4e64-9bd0-93bfd77f5c01/aenm202405729-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202405729:aenm202405729-math-0001" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202405729-math-0001.png">
               <semantics>
                  <mrow>
                     <mi>Fd</mi>
                     <mover accent="true">
                        <mn>3</mn>
                        <mo>¯</mo>
                     </mover>
                     <mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{Fd}}\bar{3}{\mathrm{m}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0054_R_d140825861e1025" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - Adv. Sci.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, the variation of atomic column intensity usually serves as an indicator of atom occupation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0055_R_d140825861e1031" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - CCS Chem">55</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0056_R_d140825861e1031" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - ChemCatChem">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the marked region, the atomic column profile exhibits a notable atomic deletion in intensity, indicating the presence of an iron vacancy. TEM image of FIS also reveals the presence of irregular and solid nanoparticles, corresponding to the SEM observation (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0002">2i</a>). As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0002">2j</a>, a set of lattice fringes with a spacing of 0.32&nbsp;nm is clearly observed, assigning to the (311) crystal plane of cubic <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/a6998a7d-09e3-45b4-bf98-d896d88ad643/aenm202405729-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202405729:aenm202405729-math-0002" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202405729-math-0002.png">
               <semantics>
                  <mrow>
                     <mi>Fd</mi>
                     <mover accent="true">
                        <mn>3</mn>
                        <mo>¯</mo>
                     </mover>
                     <mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{Fd}}\bar{3}{\mathrm{m}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. Energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDX)&nbsp;mapping images of FIS-V and FIS (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0002">2k</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information) demonstrate the homogeneous distribution of Fe, In, S, C, and N elements, indicating the well-constructed bimetallic sulfides embedded in the S/N co-doped carbon framework.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202405729-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f1de20a8-ba85-469a-a709-734bfe4da350/aenm202405729-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f1de20a8-ba85-469a-a709-734bfe4da350/aenm202405729-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/e39f0090-875d-41bd-90d0-47d96998d83b/aenm202405729-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f1de20a8-ba85-469a-a709-734bfe4da350/aenm202405729-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202405729-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202405729" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">SEM images of a–c) FIS-V and d) FIS; TEM characterizations of e–h) FIS-V and i,j) FIS; k) EDX mapping of FIS-V.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The X-ray diffraction (XRD) peaks of as-prepared In-MOF and bimetallic In-Fe-MOF are all alike and consistent with those in the reported literature (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0057_R_d140825861e1090" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - J. Mater. Sci. Technol.">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> indicating that the introduction of Fe atom does influence the crystal structure of the In-MOF. As depicted in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0003">3a</a>, the diffraction peaks of monometallic In-MOF-derived IS are indexed to the standard cubic In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> (JCPDS: 32–0456), which severs as an ideal precursor for ion substitution to synthesize FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. As anticipated, FIS exhibits sharp diffraction peaks that correspond to the standard cubic FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> (JCPDS: 33–0613). Moreover, FIS-V obtained through one-step sulfidation using bimetallic In-Fe MOF as a precursor is also characterized as a cubic FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> phase. The variation in diffraction peak intensity between FIS and FIS-V is influenced by the duration of calcination. Electron paramagnetic resonance (EPR)&nbsp;is a powerful tool to detect unpaired electrons, which are commonly presented as structural defects or vacancies. Compared to the weak signal of FIS, the stronger symmetric signal at a <i>g</i> value of 1.99 reveals the presence of more structural vacancies in FIS-V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0003">3b</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0058_R_d140825861e1124" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Chem. Eng. J.">58</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to the inductively coupled plasma optical emission spectrometer (ICP-OES)&nbsp;results, the actual molar ratio of Fe: In is 0.96: 2 and 0.87: 2 in FIS and FIS-V, respectively, demonstrating the missing iron coordination in FIS-V structure. Furthermore, positron annihilation life spectroscopy (PALS) is conducted to reveal the formed structural vacancies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0059_R_d140825861e1130" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - J. Mater. Chem. A">59</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The lifetime of <i>τ</i><sub>1</sub>&nbsp;is typically attributed to the lattice defects, such as structural vacancies (<i>τ</i><sub>v</sub>) or dislocation vacancies (<i>τ</i><sub>d</sub>), whereas&nbsp;<i>τ</i><sub>2</sub>&nbsp;is assigned to the clusters of vacancies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0060_R_d140825861e1148" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">60</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0061_R_d140825861e1148" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - Nat. Commun.">61</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0003">3d</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information), FIS-V exhibits a higher <i>τ</i><sub>1</sub>&nbsp;value (360.8&nbsp;±&nbsp;0.8&nbsp;ps) than that of FIS (356.7&nbsp;±&nbsp;0.7&nbsp;ps), indicating an increased amount of cation vacancies. Meanwhile, the <i>τ</i><sub>1</sub>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<i>τ</i><sub>2</sub>&nbsp;relative intensities of FIS-V is 97.25% and 2.75%, respectively, which suggests the dominant proportion of cationic lattice defects in FIS-V. The high-resolution Fe 2p X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS)&nbsp;spectrum of FIS-V and FIS exhibits the same profile, which can be divided as the marcasite Fe-S 2p<sub>3/2</sub>, Fe<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub>, Fe<sup>3+</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub>, and the corresponding Fe 2p<sub>1/2</sub> components, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0003">3e</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0009_R_d140825861e1186" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">9</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0062_R_d140825861e1186" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">62</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0064_R_d140825861e1186" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - Interdisciplinary Mater.">64</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, the prominent peak located at 704.1&nbsp;eV originates from the indium component (In 3p<sub>1/2</sub>), which is often misidentified as a signal of Fe 2p.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0054_R_d140825861e1193" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - Adv. Sci.">54</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0065_R_d140825861e1193" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - Mater. Today Commun.">65</a>-<a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0067" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0067_R_d140825861e1193" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - Small">67</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This signal is observed in the XPS spectrum of IS (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4a</a>, Supporting Information), further confirming the attribution of the In 3p<sub>1/2</sub> peak. Moreover, FIS-V exhibits a lower intensity of marcasite Fe-S, indicating the reduced strength of Fe─S bonds in the iron-deficient environment. The validity of this assumption is also confirmed in the high-resolution S 2p spectra. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0003">3f</a>, both S 2p spectra can be deconvoluted into the S 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and S 2p<sub>1/2</sub> peaks corresponding to the In─S, Fe─S, C─S and sulfate species, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0014_R_d140825861e1212" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Nanoscale">14</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0042_R_d140825861e1212" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Appl. Energ. Mater.">42</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0068_R_d140825861e1212" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 68 - Energy Storage Mater.">68</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0069" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0069_R_d140825861e1212" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 69 - Electrochimca Acta">69</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The lower intensities of Fe-S peaks reflect the lower content or strength of Fe─S bonds in FIS-V. Additionally, the presence of C─S bonds means successful sulfur doping in the carbon framework during the sulfuration process, facilitating the enhancement of conductivity in as-prepared composite materials.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202405729-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/9e18c8d4-6bed-4cc4-8acb-5a76c10e68ca/aenm202405729-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/9e18c8d4-6bed-4cc4-8acb-5a76c10e68ca/aenm202405729-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/60c5017e-8a81-4c23-a57a-76525ed2f471/aenm202405729-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/9e18c8d4-6bed-4cc4-8acb-5a76c10e68ca/aenm202405729-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202405729-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202405729" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XRD patterns of IS, FIS, and FIS-V; b) EPR spectra, c) molar ratio of Fe: In obtained from ICP-OES, and d) positron annihilation life spectra of FIS and FIS-V; high-resolution XPS spectrum of e) Fe 2p, f) In 3d, g) S 2p and h) N 1s; i) Fe K-edge XANES spectra of FIS, FIS-V, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, FeS, FeO and Fe foil; j) EXAFS spectra of FIS and FIS-V with the standard references Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, FeS and Fe foil; WT-EXAFS signals of k) FIS-V and l) FIS.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The incorporation of Fe element results in an increased proportion of C-N/S bonds in the C 1s spectra of FIS and FIS-V (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4b</a>, Supporting Information),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0070" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0070_R_d140825861e1257" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 70 - Nanomaterials">70</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0071_R_d140825861e1257" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 71 - Adv. Energy Mater.">71</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> indicating its dual role in regulating the electronic structure of In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>-based host material and catalyzing heterogeneous atoms doping on carbon matrix. In comparison to the In 3d spectrum of FIS, the sight shift of FIS-V peaks suggests the influence of iron-deficiency on indium valence (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0003">3g</a>). Benefited by the nitrogen-containing ligands in the In-MOF precursor, a N, S co-doped carbon framework is obtained to support the rapid electron transfer capability (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0003">3h</a>). Notably, the presence of a Fe-N<sub>x</sub> bond in FIS-V would further regulate the electronic structure and enhance the catalytic ability for facilitating the reaction kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0072" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0072_R_d140825861e1275" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 72 - ACS Energy Lett.">72</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0073" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0073_R_d140825861e1275" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 73 - Nano Lett.">73</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to the TG curve, the carbon content of FIS-V is estimated as 33.9% (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information). Besides, FIS-V also delivers a lower average electrical resistivity of 8.49 (Ω·cm) than that of FIS (13.64 Ω·cm) by a four-probe resistivity tester, which is in agreement with theoretical calculation (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information). The structural features and defect types of as-prepared samples are further determined by X-ray absorption fine structure (XAFS) analysis. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0003">3i</a>, the spectra of Fe K-edge X-ray absorption near-edge structure (XANES) reveal that the valence state of Fe in FIS-V is higher than that of FIS, which would be attributed to the iron-deficient environment inducing an increase in Fe valence state around vacant locations to maintain overall valence balance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0074" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0074_R_d140825861e1290" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 74 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">74</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Evidently, the obvious peak at 7112&nbsp;eV indicates an inclination toward a metallic electronic configuration in FIS-V,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0075" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0075_R_d140825861e1295" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 75 - Chem">75</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0076" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0076_R_d140825861e1295" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 76 - Small">76</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> due to the iron-deficient environment. Furthermore, the detailed coordination structures of Fe in FIS and FIS-V are unveiled through Fourier-transformed extended X-ray absorption fine structure (FT-EXAFS). As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0003">3j</a>, the Fe─S bond length of FIS-V and FIS at the first shell decreases from 2.18 to 2.06 Å (after phase position correction), reflecting the influence of indium on the coordination environment of iron. Notably, the intensity of Fe─S shoulder in FIS-V is lower than that of FIS, providing another powerful evidence for the presence of Fe vacancies. The wavelet transforms of EXAFS (WT-EXAFS) spectra in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0003">3k,l</a> further confirm the scattering Fe-S path while exhibiting the reduced intensity of the Fe─S bond in FIS-V.</p>
         
         <p>CR2032-type coin cells are utilized to evaluate the electrochemical performance of as-prepared samples. First, cyclic voltammetry (CV) is conducted to reveal the sodiation-desodiation behavior of FIS-V and FIS (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0004">4a</a>). During the cathodic scan, the peak ≈0.7&nbsp;V represents the formation of solid electrolyte interface (SEI) film and Na<sup>+</sup> first insertion. Notably, the larger profile and broader peak of FIS-V indicate more charge storage capability and faster reaction kinetics compared to its counterpart. The sharp peaks at 0.5 and 0.43&nbsp;V correspond to the gradual phase transformation from Na<sub>x</sub>FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> to In, Fe, and Na<sub>2</sub>S.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0033_R_d140825861e1327" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J. Colloid. Interface. Sci.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the anodic scan, the peaks at 0.8, 1.2, and 1.55&nbsp;V belong to the stepwise desodiation processes leading to the reconstruction of FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0027_R_d140825861e1337" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, the well-overlapped CV curves of FIS-V imply its high cyclic reversibility. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0004">4b</a>, the FIS-V anode exhibits the discharge/charge capacity of 725/612 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> with an initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 84.4%, which is much higher than that of FIS (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0004">4c</a>, 600/506 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). Notably, both FIS-V and FIS deliver the increased ICE compared with IS anode (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, Supporting Information, 78.4%), suggesting that the introduction of Fe promotes the reversibility of sodiation-desodiation reaction in In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>-based anodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0027_R_d140825861e1362" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, compared to the FIS electrode, the initial discharge curve of FIS-V exhibits a smoother voltage plateau, indicating accelerated reaction kinetics.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202405729-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/9203660a-87fe-416d-902c-a991b2f8fbaf/aenm202405729-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/9203660a-87fe-416d-902c-a991b2f8fbaf/aenm202405729-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/3eec8e47-2d34-4e66-a32f-8b29cc2b994a/aenm202405729-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/9203660a-87fe-416d-902c-a991b2f8fbaf/aenm202405729-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202405729-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202405729" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV curves of FIS-V and FIS in the potential range of 0.005–2.5&nbsp;V at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>; initial charge–discharge curves of b) FIS-V and c) FIS at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>; d) rate performance, e) cyclic evaluation, f) GITT curves and g) the corresponding Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient of FIS-V and FIS; h) charge–discharge curves of commercial Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode, Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>‖FIS-V full cell and FIS-V anode; i) cyclic performance and j) complex operating condition evaluation of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>‖FIS-V full cell.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <div class="paragraph-element">As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0004">4d</a>, FIS-V displays the remarkably enhanced and repeatable rate performance, achieving a specific capacity of 558, 530, 490, 458, 415, and 381 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2. 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The long-term cyclic evaluation demonstrates that FIS-V retains a high capacity of 448 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention of 85.8%, surpassing its counterparts of FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> without Fe vacancies, IS and reported In-based anodes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0004">4e</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information). Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) are conducted to reveal the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0004">4f</a>, the GITT curves of FIV-S display similar profiles as its corresponding charge–discharge curves, and with a smaller ∆E<sub>s</sub> (the voltage difference between the initial and steady state) compared to the FIS, which indicates the improved coulombic efficiency and electrochemical performance. According to the Equation&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#aenm202405729-disp-0001" title="Link to equation">1</a>),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0039_R_d140825861e1461" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Sci.">39</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0076" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0076_R_d140825861e1461" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 76 - Small">76</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0077" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0077_R_d140825861e1461" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 77 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">77</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> the D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> of FIS-V shows significantly higher values than that of FIS at various potential states, which is consistent with the DFT calculation analysis and further validates the facilitative influence of Fe vacancies on Na<sup>+</sup> transfer.
            <div class="inline-equation" id="aenm202405729-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/9378675a-9163-4565-a358-49d12a10843a/aenm202405729-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202405729:aenm202405729-math-0003" display="block" location="graphic/aenm202405729-math-0003.png">

                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>
         </div>
         
         <p>Encouraged by the outstanding electrochemical performance of FIS-V in half-cells, its application potential in full-cells is further conducted by pairing with the commercial Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0004">4h</a>, the typical charge–discharge curves of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>‖FIS-V exhibit three obvious voltage plateaus at 3.2, 1.7, and 1.35&nbsp;V at the discharge stage. The capacity and current density of full-cell are determined by considering the mass of anode material. During the cyclic evaluation, the full-cell delivers excellent cyclic stability, retaining a capacity of 445 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, with a high-capacity retention of 94.7% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0004">4i</a>). The overlapped charge–discharge curves at different cycles further demonstrate the stable electrochemical behavior of FIS-V, even in the full cells. In addition, the full-cell delivers a reversible capacity of 409, 366, 324, 278, and 236 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0004">4l</a>). Impressively, after undergoing rate testing, it maintains a high capacity of 358 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at the end of the 300th cycle (87.5% capacity retention), highlighting the potential practical applications of FIS-V in SIBs.</p>
         
         <p>In situ XRD is conducted to illustrate the sodiation/desodiation process of FIS-V. As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5a</a>, the signals belonging to the Al, Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, Be, and BeO are ascribed to the Al collector and cell window, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0010_R_d140825861e1582" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Mater.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the discharge state, the main peak of FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> changes from (311) to (222) peak, indicating an expansion of the unit cell caused by continuous Na insertion.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0078" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0078_R_d140825861e1592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 78 - Adv. Energy Mater.">78</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The diffraction peaks of Fe, Na<sub>2</sub>S, and InNa can be simultaneously observed, demonstrating the composite sodium storage mechanism involving both conversion and alloy reactions in the FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode. Moreover, the presence of Na<sub>2</sub>In<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> diffraction peaks suggests the existence of an intermediate phase for facilitating the maintenance of structural stability during the initial sodiation reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0027_R_d140825861e1611" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> At the end of the first charging state, the distinct diffraction peaks of FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> reveal the reversibility of sodium storage process.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202405729-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/243e7a92-b3b2-4975-a467-95212deac339/aenm202405729-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/243e7a92-b3b2-4975-a467-95212deac339/aenm202405729-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/fc4e299d-c67a-41a9-aa78-7dccde0b71b6/aenm202405729-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/243e7a92-b3b2-4975-a467-95212deac339/aenm202405729-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202405729-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202405729" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) In situ XRD with a 2D contour plot during the first cycle; XPS spectra of b) In 3d c) Fe 2p, d) O 1s and e) F 1s f) P 2p and g) S 2p of FIS-V and FIS electrodes after 100 cycles; h) adsorption energy; TEM images of i,j) FIS-V and k) FIS electrode after 100 cycles.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Furthermore, the cycled cells are dissected to reveal the structural evolution of the FIS-V anode. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5b</a>, the peak intensity and profile smoothness of In 3d in FIS-V surpass those of FIS. This phenomenon is also observed in Fe 2p (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5c</a>), where the intensity of In 3p<sub>1/2</sub> peak in FIS tends to significantly weaken compared to FIS-V after 100 cycles, indicating the superior structural stability of the FIS-V anode. The composition of SEI film is a crucial factor that influences the electrochemical performance of electrode material, necessitating an inorganic-rich component film. In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5d</a>, the O 1s spectra of FIS and FIS-V can be deconvoluted into five distinct components, corresponding to the Na<sub>2</sub>O, Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, polyether, inorganic P-O bond, and Na Auger, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0078" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0078_R_d140825861e1661" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 78 - Adv. Energy Mater.">78</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0079" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0079_R_d140825861e1661" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 79 - Adv. Mater.">79</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, the lower content of Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> and polyether in FIS-V suggests the presence of an inorganic-rich component SEI film,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0080" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0080_R_d140825861e1671" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 80 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">80</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which is further supported by its higher intensity of P-O peak. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5e</a>, the prominent peak in F 1s spectra is attributed to the NaF component, which is a crucial substance in a stable SEI film. The higher intensity peak of FIS-V suggests the formation of a more stable SEI film compared to its counterpart.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0081" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0081_R_d140825861e1679" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 81 - Adv. Energy Mater.">81</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The two peaks in P 2p spectra correspond to the PO<sub>x</sub> and PF<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> components, which originate from the inorganic substance in SEI film and the adsorption of electrolyte decomposition products, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5f</a>). By integrating the peak areas, the proportion of PO<sub>x</sub> in FIS-V (74.4%) is higher than that in FIS (69.6%), further indicating the inorganic-rich components in the SEI film of FIS-V. In S 2p spectra, the disappearance of the M-S bond in FIS demonstrates its significant structural degradation during the cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5g</a>). Moreover, a higher area proportion of SO<sub>x</sub> peaks (79.76% in FIS and 64.48% in FIS-V) indicates that FIS would possess a thicker SEI film.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0080" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0080_R_d140825861e1702" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 80 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">80</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, at the full charge to 2.5&nbsp;V after 100 cycles, the Nyquist plots of FIS and FIS-V present a gap in the X-axis, a semicircle, and a sloping line, representing the solution resistance (R<sub>s</sub>), charge transfer resistance (R<sub>ct</sub>) and Warburg impedance, respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0082" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0082_R_d140825861e1715" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 82 - J. Colloid. Interface. Sci.">82</a>, <a href="#aenm202405729-bib-0083" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405729-bib-0083_R_d140825861e1715" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 83 - Sci. Adv.">83</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The larger R<sub>ct</sub> in the FIS cell is ascribed to the excessive decomposition of the electrolyte for forming a thicker SEI film, thereby deteriorating the cyclic stability. DFT calculations are conducted to assess the NaF adsorption energies of Fe<sub>8</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub> and Fe<sub>7</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub>, which is a crucial component in determining the formation of stable SEI film with higher inorganic substances. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5h</a>, the lower NaF adsorption energy of Fe<sub>7</sub>In<sub>16</sub>S<sub>32</sub> (−3.07&nbsp;eV) suggests its stronger affinity toward NaF, thereby promoting the NaF deposition and facilitating the formation of a stable SEI with higher content inorganic substances.</p>
         
         <p>The SEM image of the cycled FIS-V electrode exhibits a well-maintained rod morphology with exceptional structural integrity, which can be attributed to the quasi-hollow structure derived from MOFs precursor for effectively alleviating the stress caused by volumetric expansion (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information). The cross-section SEM images of the FIS-V electrode also confirm the superior capability of alleviating volumetric expansion, as evidenced by a 17.5% increase in thickness, compared to the FIS (27.2%) and IS (114.6%) electrode (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information). Additionally, the TEM image of FIS-V displays the rod-like morphology, consisting of the SEM analysis (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5i</a>). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5j</a>, the amorphous layer surrounding the electrode corresponds to the formed SEI film. Significantly, the thickness of SEI film measures between 3–4&nbsp;nm after 100 cycles, thereby effectively enhancing the cyclic stability of FIS-V. Furthermore, the cycled FIS-V exhibits clear lattice fringes with a spacing of 0.32&nbsp;nm, belonging to the cubic FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> (311) plane. Combined with the fast Fourier transform (FFT) pattern in this region (inset of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5j</a>), the anticipated structural reversibility of FIS-V can be verified. The TEM image of cycled FIS reveals the fragmented particles, demonstrating the structural degradation after cycles (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information). Furthermore, the HRTEM image of cycled FIS exhibits an amorphous layer with a range of 10–15&nbsp;nm in thickness (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405729-fig-0005">5k</a>), suggesting the formation of thicker SEI film. The inconspicuous lattice fringes confirm its inferior structural stability during the cycles.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202405729-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202405729-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, a bimetallic In-Fe-MOF is employed to construct the thiospinel FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@N/S-C microrods with Fe vacancies (FIS-V) for the advanced SIB anode. In comparison to the Fe<sup>2+</sup> substitution approach, the bimetallic MOF precursor endows the products with notable advantages in terms of enhanced electrochemical performance and simplified preparation procedures. The presence of Fe vacancies in FeIn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>4</sub> regulates the <i>d</i>-band center of Fe and decreases the strength of the Fe-S bond, facilitating the kinetics of sodiation reaction to improve structural reversibility. Furthermore, FIS-V possesses a thin and stable SEI film with inorganic-rich components induced by the Fe vacancies. Combined with the MOF-derived porous N, S co-doped carbon matrix, FIS-V delivers the high reversible capacity of 611 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> with an increased ICE (from 78.4 to 84.3%), excellent rate capability (381 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>) and stable cyclic performance (448 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>). Additionally, the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>‖FIS-V full cells also exhibit durable cyclic performance, maintaining a high capacity of 445 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> (94.7% capacity retention) and presenting a remarkable capacity retention of 87.5% after complex cycles at different current densities. This work presents a promising strategy for regulating the structure of bimetallic sulfides as an advanced anode in sodium batteries.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">

         <div class="accordion article-accordion">
            <h2><a href="#" class="accordion__control" role="button" aria-controls="open-research-content" aria-expanded="false"><span class="section__title" id="open-research-section">Open Research</span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a></h2>
            <div class="accordion__content" role="region" aria-labelledby="open-research-section" id="open-research-content">
